<h1 itemprop="name" class="bookTitle" id="bookTitle">
      The Notebook
      <a href="/series/93822-the-notebook" class="greyText">
          (The Notebook #1)

  <span class="by smallText">by</span>
<span itemtype="http://schema.org/Person" itemscope="" itemprop="author">
<a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2345.Nicholas_Sparks" itemprop="url" class="authorName"><span itemprop="name">Nicholas Sparks</span></a> <span class="greyText">(Goodreads Author)</span>

<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17753475310343368474">Every so often a love story so captures our hearts that it becomes more than a story-it becomes an experience to remember forever. The Notebook is such a book. It is a celebration of how passion can be ageless and timeless, a tale that moves us to laughter and tears and makes us believe in true love all over again... At thirty-one, Noah Calhoun, back in coastal North Carol</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17753475310343368474">Every so often a love story so captures our hearts that it becomes more than a story-it becomes an experience to remember forever. The Notebook is such a book. It is a celebration of how passion can be ageless and timeless, a tale that moves us to laughter and tears and makes us believe in true love all over again... At thirty-one, Noah Calhoun, back in coastal North Carolina after World War II, is haunted by images of the girl he lost more than a decade earlier. At twenty-nine, socialite Allie Nelson is about to marry a wealthy lawyer, but she cannot stop thinking about the boy who long ago stole her heart. Thus begins the story of a love so enduring and deep it can turn tragedy into triumph, and may even have the power to create a miracle...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17753475310343368474">...more</a>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one! </span></div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer9978079">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3684520006533618390">I love the movie, but if you think that was sappy, do not pick up this book. I heard Nicholas Sparks had a knack for sap, but I almost drowned in it and felt no spark at all. The book was so frustratingly simple and obvious and laid out. The dialoque droned. I'll come back and add a real quote, but it was something like this:<br /><br />"Do you want to stay for dinner?" he asked, wondering what she would say.<br />"Okay," she said, and than asked, "What should we eat?"<br />"Crabs," he said. <br />She never had crabs. They b</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3684520006533618390">I love the movie, but if you think that was sappy, do not pick up this book. I heard Nicholas Sparks had a knack for sap, but I almost drowned in it and felt no spark at all. The book was so frustratingly simple and obvious and laid out. The dialoque droned. I'll come back and add a real quote, but it was something like this:<br /><br />"Do you want to stay for dinner?" he asked, wondering what she would say.<br />"Okay," she said, and than asked, "What should we eat?"<br />"Crabs," he said. <br />She never had crabs. They began to cook the crabs... etc. <br /><br />There is a "quiver in his loins" when he sees her in her transparent white dress as well. <br /><br />Oh and "the two become one" when they make love.<br /><br />And then she is forced to leave when her fiance pays a surprise visit to down and she struggles to drive through her tears, but fights through the blurry vision because she is a strong woman like her mother... lalalalala. Could the book be any more contrived and gimicky? Who rated this above a one? And please enlighten me.<br /><br />Gag, gag, awful writing, what a frustrating bore. He left nothing to the imagination. Unless you like getting dumber by the minute, don't pick this one up. </span>

  <a href="/user/show/223106-stacey" class="left imgcol" title="Stacey"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1186423400p2/223106.jpg" alt="Stacey" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/4157672?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 06, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/223106-stacey" class="user" title="Stacey">Stacey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/336903.The_Notebook" title="Hardcover 9780446520805" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/223106-stacey?shelf=gag-me-with-a-spoon" class="actionLinkLite">gag-me-with-a-spoon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer4157672">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1079780932233925282">I read this book on a train from Italy to somewhere else in Europe after graduating from college. I was unfortunate enough to be forced to buy it because there were no other English Language novels to choose from.<br /><br />I know this is a beloved book, by a beloved author, but if I could give it any sort of negative rating, I would. The "Gag me with a spoon" category is almost too kind. My apologies to any one who likes Nicholas Sparks - if you're able to find the genius in his writing, more power to you</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1079780932233925282">I read this book on a train from Italy to somewhere else in Europe after graduating from college. I was unfortunate enough to be forced to buy it because there were no other English Language novels to choose from.<br /><br />I know this is a beloved book, by a beloved author, but if I could give it any sort of negative rating, I would. The "Gag me with a spoon" category is almost too kind. My apologies to any one who likes Nicholas Sparks - if you're able to find the genius in his writing, more power to you!<br /><br />When I heard the plot - an old man is reliving his personal history with the love of his life as she suffers from dementia - I had much hope for a touching story. Esh - I was sorely disappointed.<br /><br />My favorite memory is reading the scene between the two young (and I'm assuming attractive) lovers...they are in a boat on a lake, romantic setting, yes? It starts to rain. She's wearing a white dress. "We have to get you inside where it's warm...better remove those wet clothes, you'll catch a cold..." Commence eye-rolling now.<br /><br />After reading the book, I passed it on to my now husband, who was also on the train. Keep in mind, there were no other English options! He starts to comment, "Oh, they're on the lake in a boat...okay, it's raining...oh geeze, why do you girls read this crap?"<br /><br />And that's what I think about this book...why would anyone read this (unless there were no other choices)?!?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1079780932233925282">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1496724905">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1496724905" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/14596170-lola" class="left imgcol" title="Lola "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451614011p2/14596170.jpg" alt="Lola " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1496724905?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 07, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/14596170-lola" class="user" title="Lola ">Lola </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15931.The_Notebook" title="Hardcover 9780553816716" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/14596170-lola?shelf=soul-mates" class="actionLinkLite">soul-mates</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/14596170-lola?shelf=cheesy-romance" class="actionLinkLite">cheesy-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/14596170-lola?shelf=social-class" class="actionLinkLite">social-class</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1496724905">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3655090841005367086"><br />I’m just gonna say it: <strong>I expected less</strong>.<br /><br />Not being inexperienced in the reading of Nicholas Sparks novels, I somewhat knew this book would contain tons and tons of corny and cheesy replies and gestures. But <strong>NOT</strong> in every. single. paragraph. I’m not one to discard the idea of soul mates, after all the young adult readings that I have done, but when something is too wonderful and perfect, it’s more annoying than cute. So there is too much of that.<br /><br />Also, the plot is so weirdly shaped. It starts with No</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3655090841005367086"><br />I’m just gonna say it: <strong>I expected less</strong>.<br /><br />Not being inexperienced in the reading of Nicholas Sparks novels, I somewhat knew this book would contain tons and tons of corny and cheesy replies and gestures. But <strong>NOT</strong> in every. single. paragraph. I’m not one to discard the idea of soul mates, after all the young adult readings that I have done, but when something is too wonderful and perfect, it’s more annoying than cute. So there is too much of that.<br /><br />Also, the plot is so weirdly shaped. It starts with Noah as an elderly, in the first person, then it continues in the 3rd person with Noah in his thirties, and it finally ends with elderly Noah in the first person again. I know why the author did that and it’s pretty ingenious when you globally think about it… but reading it is a different story. The 3rd person part of the story is cut at the most decisive moment and that is utterly outraging. <br /><br />Moreover, when Noah sees Allie again, she is engaged to a super rich attorney. That super rich attorney, to whom I forgot the name of, is madly stressed out when he discovers that Allie has been with Noah the whole time she claimed to needing time to make some purchases in a specific city. So what does he do? He runs to her and tries to win her back! But does he ever turn against Noah? Bah! Noah is an angel, how can anyone despise him?<br /><br />And finally, the mother. Allie’s mother. She disapproved of them as a couple when they were in their teen years, but now more than a dozen years later she doesn’t even blink when she learns Allie has gone back to Noah and never tries to talk Allie into going back to her super rich attorney. So not realistic. <br /><br /><strong>Basically, this book is made of rainbows and sunshine. <br />Not my favorite combination. <br />I expected less of that.<br />Sigh. </strong><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3655090841005367086">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

In fact, I LOVED the movie and watched it before reading this. In the movie, the characters of Noah and Allie had more intensity and passion. It is one of those rare moments, for me, when the movie was better than the book.<br /><br />There are some great quotes in this book though. These were my favourite:<br /><br /><em>"I am a common man with common thoughts, and I've led a common life. There are no monuments dedic</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11476619138396434665"><strong>4 Stars</strong> - <em>
  <strong>Also reviewed at: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://ladyjaynesreadingden.blogspot.com/">Lady Jayne's Reading Den</a></strong>
</em><br /><br />Sweet and romantic, but I liked the movie much more. In fact, I LOVED the movie and watched it before reading this. In the movie, the characters of Noah and Allie had more intensity and passion. It is one of those rare moments, for me, when the movie was better than the book.<br /><br />There are some great quotes in this book though. These were my favourite:<br /><br /><em>"I am a common man with common thoughts, and I've led a common life. There are no monuments dedicated to me and my name will soon be forgotten, but I've loved another with all my heart and soul, and to me, this has always been enough."<br /><br />"We sit silently and watch the world around us. This has taken a lifetime to learn. It seems only the old are able to sit next to one another and not say anything and still feel content. The young, brash and impatient, must always break the silence. It is a waste, for silence is pure. Silence is holy. It draws people together because only those who are comfortable with each other can sit without speaking." <br /><br />"The best love is the kind that awakens the soul and makes us reach for more, that plants a fire in our hearts and brings peace to our minds, and that's what you've given to me..."<br /><br />"We fell in love, despite our differences, and once we did, something rare and beautiful was created. For me, love like that has only happened once, and that's why every minute we spent together has been seared in my memory. I'll never forget a single moment of it."<br /><br />"So it's not gonna be easy. It's going to be really hard; we're gonna have to work at this everyday, but I want to do that because I want you. I want all of you, forever, everyday. You and me... everyday."<br /><br />"I love you. I am who I am because of you. You are every reason, every hope, and every dream I've ever had, and no matter what happens to us in the future, everyday we are together is the greatest day of my life. I will always be yours."</em><br /><br /><img width="385" height="270" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380323408i/690614.jpg" /><br /><br /><img width="385" height="270" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380323408i/690615.jpg" /><br /><br /><img width="385" height="295" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380323408i/690616.jpg" /><br /><p>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_125850223">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125850223" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy" class="left imgcol" title="Kat Kennedy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1394913263p2/3270188.jpg" alt="Kat Kennedy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/125850223?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 31, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy" class="user" title="Kat Kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15931.The_Notebook" title="Hardcover 9780553816716" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews" class="actionLinkLite">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=romance-romance-romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance-romance-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer125850223">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12915667315946197938">Have you ever come across something so undeniably cute that you feel like you may be crushed by the weight of squee that’s about to explode from you chest.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" alt="”cute”/" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340385i/696789.jpg" /><br />Kind of like when you see this?<br /><br />That’s what reading The Notebook was like. The romantic tone of The Notebook was both its greatest asset and biggest downfall. Nobody wants to be crushed by squee anymore <br />than they want to drown in their own tears and The Notebook wants to destroy you. Never doubt that. Whether it’s leaching your bodily liquids o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12915667315946197938">Have you ever come across something so undeniably cute that you feel like you may be crushed by the weight of squee that’s about to explode from you chest.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" alt="”cute”/" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340385i/696789.jpg" /><br />Kind of like when you see this?<br /><br />That’s what reading The Notebook was like. The romantic tone of The Notebook was both its greatest asset and biggest downfall. Nobody wants to be crushed by squee anymore <br />than they want to drown in their own tears and The Notebook wants to destroy you. Never doubt that. Whether it’s leaching your bodily liquids out of you until you resemble The Ice Man or boring you to death. <br /><br />Really, those are the only two options you’ve got with this book. Who can stand to see something as cute as that kitten up there all day every day? You need something not so cute to break up the boredom. Similarly, in The Notebook, the long, romantic verses filled with poetry and stunning imagery will ultimately become tiresome the longer you read it.<br /><br />Probably it’s just me. In case you haven’t figured it out, I’m not exactly the most romantic person out there. In my relationship it’s my husband who is the romantic. He’s the one that makes me breakfast in bed every single morning and puts a rose from the garden on my tray. He’s the one that calls me to see how my day’s gone and sends me soppy, romantic messages. <br /><br />If you’re a sentimental, sweet kind of person (two adjectives nobody has ever applied to me) then I’m sure you’d like this book and it would do you justice. For those who like a little more “action” in the literary sack then this book may tend to waffle on and be overly mushy.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" alt="”horrifying”/" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340385i/696790.jpg" /><br />Now THAT’S more like it! <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12915667315946197938">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer6126296020234628188">This is my favorite love story ever. It shows what true soul mates are. (I also loved the movie as much as the book.) If you don't cry when you read this then something is wrong with you. I think that you can love someone like ally did the lawyer, but only true love with your soul mate like with Noah. People who don't like this book have never truely been loved, because if you have it hits home.<br /><br />Here are a few of my favorite quotes from the book:<br /><br />"I am a common man with common thoughts, and I've l</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6126296020234628188">This is my favorite love story ever. It shows what true soul mates are. (I also loved the movie as much as the book.) If you don't cry when you read this then something is wrong with you. I think that you can love someone like ally did the lawyer, but only true love with your soul mate like with Noah. People who don't like this book have never truely been loved, because if you have it hits home.<br /><br />Here are a few of my favorite quotes from the book:<br /><br />"I am a common man with common thoughts, and I've led a common life. There are no monuments dedicated to me and my name will soon be forgotten, but I've loved another with all my heart and soul, and to me, this has always been enough." <br /><br />"We sit silently and watch the world around us. This has taken a lifetime to learn. It seems only the old are able to sit next to one another and not say anything and still feel content. The young, brash and impatient, must always break the silence. It is a waste, for silence is pure. Silence is holy. It draws people together because only those who are comfortable with each other can sit without speaking."</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8164475349508501489">Vanessa bought me this book after I watched <em>Fracture</em> and developed a serious crush on Ryan Gosling. Well, that led me to this movie and, unfortunately, this book. How does this man have a career as a writer?! Who is paying him to write stories with the most obvious choices in plot/dialogue/decisions. Wow. Lowest common denominator.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Tracy Rupple, and no one else. </span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/682651-carolyn?shelf=almost-a-complete-waste-of-time" class="actionLinkLite">almost-a-complete-waste-of-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer10396867">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18016211034637552701">I read this book because my sister loved it. It made me sad. Not because it was a sad story, but because it was so poorly written. <br /><br />This Sparks character had a fantastic idea for a story, a truly painful and passionate story of love and devotion. But the book? It was like my 14 year old nephew watched this brilliant movie, then tried to write about it on his myspace blog. It was butchered by an appalling lack adjectives and an appalling lack of emotion. Sad. <br /><br />The fact that so many people are willi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18016211034637552701">I read this book because my sister loved it. It made me sad. Not because it was a sad story, but because it was so poorly written. <br /><br />This Sparks character had a fantastic idea for a story, a truly painful and passionate story of love and devotion. But the book? It was like my 14 year old nephew watched this brilliant movie, then tried to write about it on his myspace blog. It was butchered by an appalling lack adjectives and an appalling lack of emotion. Sad. <br /><br />The fact that so many people are willing to overlook Sparks' lack of creativity and inability to, well, write, is also sad. Sad, I say. <br /><br />Sorry Tracy. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_29746221">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29746221" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1253753-muphyn" class="left imgcol" title="Muphyn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1226965874p2/1253753.jpg" alt="Muphyn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/29746221?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 28, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1253753-muphyn" class="user" title="Muphyn">Muphyn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2005220.The_Notebook" title="Audio CD 9781600242564" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Muphyn by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1250419-miss-bookiverse">Miss Bookiverse</a>
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1253753-muphyn?shelf=audiobook" class="actionLinkLite">audiobook</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1253753-muphyn?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1253753-muphyn?shelf=beach-reading" class="actionLinkLite">beach-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer29746221">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11149336832606755524">Besides the awful writing style (just to mention unimaginative, spiritless and full of clichés), I found the story just a little too contrived and far too predictable. I couldn't get over the premise where Noah and Allie meet when they are teenagers, spend one summer together and meet again after 14 years to realise they are still utterly in love?! What?!<br /><br />It irritated me to no end that Sparks felt the need to not leave anything unexplained, describing things in excruciating detail, boring me but</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11149336832606755524">Besides the awful writing style (just to mention unimaginative, spiritless and full of clichés), I found the story just a little too contrived and far too predictable. I couldn't get over the premise where Noah and Allie meet when they are teenagers, spend one summer together and meet again after 14 years to realise they are still utterly in love?! What?!<br /><br />It irritated me to no end that Sparks felt the need to not leave anything unexplained, describing things in excruciating detail, boring me but more so putting me off reading any of his other books. In the end it just felt like it was dragging on and on and on - I just wanted it to end.<br /><br />Also, since I listened to the audio version I must say that the choice for the reader of the audio book isn't the most brilliant one. His voice is kind of suited for the old Noah but his imitation of a young Allie is just really off-putting. Plus, he's got that kind of voice that makes me want to fall asleep straight away. Combine that with the terrible style and plot, this book can only be described as indigestible. No more Nicholas Sparks for me, thank you!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11149336832606755524">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_19894037">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19894037" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1069403-abby" class="left imgcol" title="Abby"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1299018718p2/1069403.jpg" alt="Abby" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/19894037?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 10, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1069403-abby" class="user" title="Abby">Abby</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15931.The_Notebook" title="Hardcover 9780553816716" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer19894037">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4244870127166509973">So, I didn't love this book, even though every other girl on planet earth does. Here's the deal: it's an old guy at the end of his life, showing how undyingly committed and in love he is with his elderly wife, who is dying of Alzheimer's. Sweet, right? Except here is how he shows his love: every day, he reads her the story of their love. It involves hooking up as teenagers, then being apart without communication for years and years, yet yearning for one another while sleeping around with other p</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4244870127166509973">So, I didn't love this book, even though every other girl on planet earth does. Here's the deal: it's an old guy at the end of his life, showing how undyingly committed and in love he is with his elderly wife, who is dying of Alzheimer's. Sweet, right? Except here is how he shows his love: every day, he reads her the story of their love. It involves hooking up as teenagers, then being apart without communication for years and years, yet yearning for one another while sleeping around with other people, then getting back together to fornicate like crazy and cheat on her fiance and break up her soon to be wedding. If that is not eternal and undying love, I don't know what is. There is no way you can go wrong picking a life partner if you are horny and running away from responsibility and commitment, as this book clearly shows. That is the only way to find a man who will love you and change your diapers for you when you get old.<br /><br />Okay, so he wasn't changing her diapers, but you get the point. I try to go with the romance of the book, and it is romantic in the eldery love sort of way (hence the 3 stars, because I figure eventually they grew up), but I can't help but think the main characters are sleazy. The end. Throw tomatoes at me now.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4244870127166509973">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light" class="user" title="Crystal Starr Light">Crystal Starr Light</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/103506.The_Notebook" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Crystal Starr Light by: </span>
      Jane
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=so-bad-it-s-good" class="actionLinkLite">so-bad-it-s-good</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=hello-my-name-is-mary-sue" class="actionLinkLite">hello-my-name-is-mary-sue</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=idiot-protagonist" class="actionLinkLite">idiot-protagonist</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=buddy-reads" class="actionLinkLite">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=i-should-know-better" class="actionLinkLite">i-should-know-better</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=book-to-movie" class="actionLinkLite">book-to-movie</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=abs" class="actionLinkLite">abs</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=editor-wanted" class="actionLinkLite">editor-wanted</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=is-this-for-real" class="actionLinkLite">is-this-for-real</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=gonna-cry-cry-cry" class="actionLinkLite">gonna-cry-cry-cry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer112825631">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14350813945519780695">Well, that's one author I can cross off my "to-read" list.<br /><br />Noah and Allie fell in love one summer when he was 17 and she 15. She leaves, and fourteen years pass before Allie, now engaged, returns to Noah. Are they still in love? Will she marry her over-working fiance, with whom she shares a passionless relationship and who keeps her from pursuing her passion of art? Or will she choose Noah, the boy she spent a grand total of one summer with and lost her virginity to (and hasn't had sex with anoth</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14350813945519780695">Well, that's one author I can cross off my "to-read" list.<br /><br />Noah and Allie fell in love one summer when he was 17 and she 15. She leaves, and fourteen years pass before Allie, now engaged, returns to Noah. Are they still in love? Will she marry her over-working fiance, with whom she shares a passionless relationship and who keeps her from pursuing her passion of art? Or will she choose Noah, the boy she spent a grand total of one summer with and lost her virginity to (and hasn't had sex with another man in the entire 14 years they've been apart)?<br /><br />I see people enjoying this for primarily two reason:<br /><br />1. You adore sappy romances where you can predict the plot from the beginning and have to keep a box of tissues nearby for the monsoon of tears that will be spilled. BONUS: You love the "Greatest Love of All Ages" ending with the couple in "present day" as 80 year-olds gasping on their death beds, clinging to each other's hands.<br /><br />2. You love to participate in Bad Book Buddy Reads with an amazing compatriot. You love to groan as the plot points are written in big crayon pages before they appear, roll your eyes at the overwrought descriptions of love, and wince at Trio of Terrible Writing, Cardboard Characters, and Zero Subtlety.<br /><br />Guess which one I was?<br /><br />This book was bad; bad as in "so good it's bad" category. Meaning, perfect for Bad Book Buddy Reads. And I was not disappointed - this book was a gold mine of snarkable material.<br /><br />The characters are so flat, they are almost invisible. Noah is the Rugged Poet (who writes no poetry), giving him the duo combination of being Deep/Intellectual but also a man who works with his hands (he WORKS for a living gorrammit!). Allie is a Passionate Free-Spirit, who loves to paint and is therefore Deep and Artsy. The rest of the characters (what few of them even exist) are even worse (if that is possible); Lon is the Foil, Anne, Allie's mom, is the Voice of Inspiration, Gus is the Person of Color (no seriously, there is no reason he appears in this book). I get that this book is a mere 213 pages long in my edition, but come on! Fill the world with some color, why don't ya?<br /><br />I was surprised at the progression of what passes for "story". I saw the movie, so I remember there was quite a bit of build-up between teenaged Allie and Noah along with the older people. The book totally skips over ANY sort of relationship building between the teenaged protagonists and instead starts the story with a HUGE backstory dump with Noah at 31 and Allie at 29! The problem is, we have spent NO TIME developing their romantic feelings for each other; instead, Allie is back to see Noah after 14 years!<br /><br />By the way, if Noah and Allie were REALLY so deeply in love, why did it take them FOURTEEN YEARS to reunite? Why were they THAT surprised when Anne withheld Noah's letters (come on, Allie's parents weren't shy in letting Noah know they didn't like him!)? Noah tries ONCE in the 14 years to see Allie; that's it! If I'm going to buy this is the Greatest Love Story of All Time (which I don't), I need to see them pursuing it.<br /><br />As for the "Greatest Love Story of All Time" - laughable. As I said, there is no chemistry between the two. Sparks relies on TELLING us (frequently!) how his characters burn for each other. That is NOT chemistry; that is a summary.<br /><br />Last thing: I could not believe how awful the writing was. It was so boring! So simple! So fraught with telling and not showing. And I even spotted some grammar errors (tenses changing in mid-sentence and some unclear pronoun usage).<br /><br />There isn't very many times I say this, but the movie was lightyears better than the book (and I wasn't even that big of a fan of the movie!). Rachel McAdams and Ryan Gosling did a great job at personifying the characters and, most importantly, conveying the Greatest Love of All Time. I guess you can give Sparks credit for being able to write a concept that would make a good movie, but when I read a book, I have certain criteria: namely characters, plot, writing. I also hate to say this, but some of the books I've really ranted against (*cough*Danse Macabre by LKH*cough*) look much better against the poor quality of this book.<br /><br />If you are curious about this book, watch the movie. If you are a big sucker for sappy romances or love to snark with buddies, pick this book up!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14350813945519780695">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_600083629">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600083629" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2679341-jane" class="left imgcol" title="Jane"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442635072p2/2679341.jpg" alt="Jane" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/600083629?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 02, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2679341-jane" class="user" title="Jane">Jane</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/103506.The_Notebook" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer600083629">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15056936170568246682">Where I got the book: I have absolutely no idea what this was doing on the Shelf of Shame. I'm really hoping it was a freebie from some event, because seriously, I wouldn't have bought it would I? Another Bad Book Buddy Read with <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>.<br /><br />Bottom line:<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400844ra/777261.gif" /><br /><br />Well, there's no accounting for taste, and if you like sappy Twoo Luv stories this is your man. My mileage varied, mostly because I was reading critically with ALL my teeth and claws out, so I'll forgive you if you enjoyed it because yeah</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15056936170568246682">Where I got the book: I have absolutely no idea what this was doing on the Shelf of Shame. I'm really hoping it was a freebie from some event, because seriously, I wouldn't have bought it would I? Another Bad Book Buddy Read with <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>.<br /><br />Bottom line:<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400844ra/777261.gif" /><br /><br />Well, there's no accounting for taste, and if you like sappy Twoo Luv stories this is your man. My mileage varied, mostly because I was reading critically with ALL my teeth and claws out, so I'll forgive you if you enjoyed it because yeah, I can see where the enjoyment could happen.<br /><br />My emotions changed as I read through this novel. They were, in order, Incredulity, Boredom and Depression. <br /><br /><strong>Incredulity</strong><br /><br />Well, THAT got off to a good start when I realized that pretty much the entire novel was going to be a flashback.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419080ra/830424.gif" /><br /><br />And increased exponentially when I encountered clichés such as the poetry-book-that-stopped-a-bullet and girl-undresses-in-front-of-mirror.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379790585i/538798.jpg" /><br /><br />This is the scene-setting exposition part of the story, which continues for an alarming 38 pages but really should have been much longer, because it's a sketch of a teenage love story (yawn) with parental opposition (YAWN) and How The War Matured Me.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419080ra/830425.gif" /><br /><br />And of course Noah is a gentle poet who likes to take things slooooooowly and commune with Nature, sort of like Walt Whitman with less hair (Whitman is liberally quoted, which vexed me because quoting poetry in novels is a pet peeve of mine. Also song lyrics.)<br /><br /><strong>Boredom</strong><br /><br />The yawns set in big time once we got into the Twoo Luv story of how Allie decides to cheat on her fiancé by looking up her old boyfriend, making sure her dress gets REALLY WET so that her nipples stand out like hard little diamonds or something, and then rubbing her hands all over Noah's chest. Oh yeah, and suggesting he crack open a bottle just in case her inhibitions don't drop low enough.<br /><br />This, naturally, leads to a massive bonkathon extending over several days.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/450048.gif" /><br /><br />After which Allie, who should pretty much be unable to walk by now, actually has the gall to do the it's-not-you-it's-me speech and LEAVE. Only to be bounced back by an even MORE clichéd scene involving Mom and, I swear I'm not making this up, the words Follow Your Heart.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419080ra/830426.gif" /><br /><br /><strong>Depression</strong><br /><br />And then the story jumps forward half a century and everyone's dying which SHOULD cheer me up, given what I think about these two, but in fact it reminds me that all Twoo Luv stories pretty much end this way. There's a REASON why we usually end with a wedding, you know. At my age I do NOT need reminding that if we're lucky we'll end up holding each other's arthritic hands in a nursing home.<br /><br />And what really gets me is that of course they've lived wildly successful artistic lives because OF COURSE Noah has reawakened the artist in Allie that was stomped on by Life and she's become famous. Even though the Allie we see in the backstory is just a bundle of sexual and emotional neediness with none of the drive and passion of a real artist. I mean if she were that great she'd be producing art without Noah having to tell her to do it, right? And then when we jump forward she's completely lost the plot anyway, so basically Allie remains entirely devoid of character. And Noah's just Wet Poet Type, Standard Issue.<br /><br />Did I say earlier that I can see why people enjoy this book? Well, yes. If you like stories without much depth that are engineered to get the tears flowing and make you feel all AHHHHH at the end, grab a box of tissues and dig in. On second thought, watch the movie because I believe it may be better. Oh look, here it is!<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419080ra/830427.gif" /><br /><br />Yep, its all wet.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15056936170568246682">...more</a>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8150013224703528899">I simply adore this review! I have never had a single urge to watch a Nicholas Sparks movie and I sure as hell haven't had the urge to read any of his books. (I am the furthest away from being a "Twoo Wuv" kind of person.) I can't believe the guy is such a best-seller and have no idea how he managed to get even one of his books made into a movie. Then again, his writing is insipid and banal enough to appeal to most Hollywood executives. And ain't that depressing.</span>

    <a href="/user/show/2679341-jane" style="font-weight:bold">Jane</a>

      
<span id="freeTextContainer12497280647498066592">I don't think you have to be a great writer to come up with stories that translate well to film. Sparks obviously has the knack of writing 'film-ready</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12497280647498066592">I don't think you have to be a great writer to come up with stories that translate well to film. Sparks obviously has the knack of writing 'film-ready' material, and good luck to him. Many of my favorite writers don't get their books made into movies or get them substantially changed because the film industry can't do justice to their subtlety.<br /><br />Still can't imagine myself watching his movies, although my oldest daughter is a fan.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12497280647498066592">...more</a>

    <br />

    <span class="xhrCommentFooter greyText">
       4 de May 05:46
    </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_2070876">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2070876" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/100282-colleen" class="left imgcol" title="Colleen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1259735918p2/100282.jpg" alt="Colleen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/2070876?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 18, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/100282-colleen" class="user" title="Colleen">Colleen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15931.The_Notebook" title="Hardcover 9780553816716" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Romantics, family of Alzheimer's</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer2070876">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13344276684188683984">As an author, I learned that this romantic, simple style is not my cup of tea. Although I enjoy cheesy comedies (the work of Capra springs to mind), I don't yearn to write them myself. The original love story of this novel was a little too pat and plain-- it was too clear that this was the love of a lifetime. Perhaps I'm jaded, but I really think a lifetime of love is more irritating-- after all, no two people can be absolutely perfect for each other. In fact, that irritation and friction, and l</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13344276684188683984">As an author, I learned that this romantic, simple style is not my cup of tea. Although I enjoy cheesy comedies (the work of Capra springs to mind), I don't yearn to write them myself. The original love story of this novel was a little too pat and plain-- it was too clear that this was the love of a lifetime. Perhaps I'm jaded, but I really think a lifetime of love is more irritating-- after all, no two people can be absolutely perfect for each other. In fact, that irritation and friction, and learning how to live with each other is what impresses me so much about long term relationships. I'm amazed that my parents are still together 29 years later because I know they've annoyed the hell out of each other-- and yet they were willing to work through that frustration because they believed their relationship (and our family) was worth it. The writing style in the beginning of the novel reminded me of my own writing during high school-- that rush of first love, that hope that you've found that one person to complete you and make your life worthwhile.<br /><br />For me, the most interesting, compelling part of The Notebook was the last segment. (If you haven't read the book, be aware that rest of this review will contain spoilers.) When the main character's love for his wife of forty-nine years triumphs even through Alzheimer's relentless blanket of memories, I was inspired. More than their love for each other, and the miracle that was their relationship, I was touched by Noah's willingness to live life in the present moment. At the end of their life together, Noah's goal each day is to fall in love with his wife again, even though she doesn't remember him. Even if he never sees that flash of recognition in her eyes, he is satisfied, as shown by this passage:<br /><br />There is beauty where we sit this afternoon, Allie and I. This is the pinnacle of my life. They are here at the creek: the birds, the geese, my friends. Their bodies float on the cool water, which reflects bits and pieces of their colors and make them seem larger than they really are. Allie too is taken in by their wonder, and little by little we get to know each other again.<br /><br />My goal is to say and truly believe that line in the middle every day: "This is the pinnacle of my life." That is the best lesson of the novel: to find happiness in simply being alive and appreciating the beauty and love around us.<br /><br />(What? I read a cheesy book! You'd BETTER expect a cheesy review!) <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13344276684188683984">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_47142785">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47142785" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1746727-arlene" class="left imgcol" title="Arlene"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" alt="Arlene" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/47142785?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 28, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1746727-arlene" class="user" title="Arlene">Arlene</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/392848.The_Notebook" title="Paperback 9780751538915" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2009" class="actionLinkLite">read-2009</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=adult" class="actionLinkLite">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer47142785">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14937260637478885387">The Notebook by Nicholas Sparks is a story about two teenagers from opposite sides of the track who meet one fateful summer and fall in love for a lifetime. This novel was engaging and steady paced. I was able to read it in one sitting as I was drawn into the lives of Noah and Allie. Nicholas Sparks has created a poignant story about two people who try to recapture the love they once shared despite the passage of time.<br /><br />Noah Calhoun is a simple boy with simple dreams. He loves poetry, his life in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14937260637478885387">The Notebook by Nicholas Sparks is a story about two teenagers from opposite sides of the track who meet one fateful summer and fall in love for a lifetime. This novel was engaging and steady paced. I was able to read it in one sitting as I was drawn into the lives of Noah and Allie. Nicholas Sparks has created a poignant story about two people who try to recapture the love they once shared despite the passage of time.<br /><br />Noah Calhoun is a simple boy with simple dreams. He loves poetry, his life in a small town, and a girl that was never meant to be his. Allie Nelson is accustomed to a life of riches and luxury, but she desires much more for herself. She loves art, music and spending time with a boy her parents do not approve of. As they explore their love for one another during their summer together, they realize that theirs is a love meant to last a lifetime. However, circumstances pull them apart for over 14 years and they are faced with trying to find a way to get back what they once had.<br /><br />I enjoyed the story, but I feel the author could have spent a little more time telling the readers about Noah and Allie’s reunion and a little more of what they went through to make a life for themselves. It was interesting to experience this story through the eyes of Noah as he enters the last chapters of his life. <br /><br />Compare Book to the Movie<br /><br />I’ve never seen the movie nor read the book, so it was enjoyable to do both back to back. After finishing the book in one sitting, I watched the DVD and was immediately able to compare the differences between the two. I feel the book was well written and the movie did a great job of bringing the main events to screen. <br /><br />One of the differences I noticed was the encounter between Allie and Martha. Martha was a love interest of Noah that never fully developed because he could not bring himself to move on. In the book, Martha leaves Noah well before Allie comes back into Noah’s life. In the book, they break up after Noah and Allie spend the night together, so obviously the timing was off, but it still worked well.<br /><br />Another difference I noticed was the way the movie depicted Noah and Allie’s relationship as somewhat volatile. They fought and told each other on several occasions that they hated each other, when that never happened in the book. In the book, their love was perfect and steady. In the movie they fought quite a bit and their breakup in the movie was disheartening, which didn’t happen that way in the book. So there were differences in their character development between both.<br /><br />The main difference between the book and the movie was the ending. As that would be a big spoiler for this review, I will not provide a detailed account, but let’s just say I felt the ending in the movie was more appropriate for this storyline.<br /><br />Overall, I enjoyed both the movie and the book and I’m glad I chose this for my reading challenge.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14937260637478885387">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8805295865251883388">In the end, Noah and Allie are in their eighties and Allie suffers from Alzheimers. Noah reads to her everyday about their life and love in the hopes of rekindling a memory of what they shared. <br /><br />Well with Alz, that's impossible as it's a degenerative disease, and once you forget, you can't remember. But against the odds, Noah helps Allie remember their life and she calls him by his name and tells him how much she loves him. That means alot to him because for the past four years, he's become a stranger to her and it breaks his heart. In the book, it's an HEA.<br /><br />In the movie, it's pretty much the same thing, she remembers him, but they die at the end holding each other's hands. :(<br /><br />I like the book's character and storyline development, but I feel the movie's ending was more appropriate.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/35417-tara" class="user" title="Tara">Tara</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer470503">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5712408212591000144"><strong>Favorite Quotes</strong><br /><br />I suppose [my life] has most resembled a blue chip stock: fairly stable, more ups than downs, and gradually trending upward over time. A good buy, a lucky buy, and I've learned that not everyone can say that about his life.<br /><br />"A living poem" had always been the words that came to mind when he tried to describe her to others.<br /><br />Our lives can't be measured by our final years, of this I am sure.<br /><br />We sit silently and watch the world around us. This has taken a lifetime to learn. It seems only</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5712408212591000144"><strong>Favorite Quotes</strong><br /><br />I suppose [my life] has most resembled a blue chip stock: fairly stable, more ups than downs, and gradually trending upward over time. A good buy, a lucky buy, and I've learned that not everyone can say that about his life.<br /><br />"A living poem" had always been the words that came to mind when he tried to describe her to others.<br /><br />Our lives can't be measured by our final years, of this I am sure.<br /><br />We sit silently and watch the world around us. This has taken a lifetime to learn. It seems only the old are able to sit next to one another and not say anything and still feel content. The young, brash and impatient, must always break the silence. It is a waste, for silence is pure. Silence is holy. It draws people together because only those who are comfortable with each other can sit without speaking. This is the great paradox.<br /><br />And I learned what is obvious to a child. That life is simply a collection of little lives, each lived one day at a time. That each day should be spent finding beauty in flowers and poetry and talking to animals. That a day spent with dreaming and sunsets and refreshing breezes cannot be bettered. But most of all, I learned that life is about sitting on benches next to ancient creeks with my hand on her knee and sometimes, on god days, for falling in love.<br /><br />It is life, I think, to watch the water. A man can learn so many things.<br /><br />And when her lips meet mine, I feel a strange tingling I have never felt before…and suddenly a miracle…and I discover a forgotten paradise, unchanged all this time, ageless like the stars. I feel the warmth of her body, and…I allow myself to slip away. I close my eyes and become a mighty ship in churning waters, strong and fearless, and she is my sails.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14877087412319584279">No sé por donde comenzar a describir este libro. Pero bueno, lo intentaré.<br />Mi amado Sparks, otra vez, logro cautivarme con sus historias de amor. Aunque en este libro, él, maneja un romance que a mí ya se me hes un poco difícil de entender, ya que todo ocurre más precipitadamente que en los otros libros que he leído de él, pero aun así logra convencerme totalmente de que ese tipo de amor y romance puede ocurrir. Y es que sinceramente, este hombre llega a escribir una pagina del porque los hombre</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14877087412319584279">No sé por donde comenzar a describir este libro. Pero bueno, lo intentaré.<br />Mi amado Sparks, otra vez, logro cautivarme con sus historias de amor. Aunque en este libro, él, maneja un romance que a mí ya se me hes un poco difícil de entender, ya que todo ocurre más precipitadamente que en los otros libros que he leído de él, pero aun así logra convencerme totalmente de que ese tipo de amor y romance puede ocurrir. Y es que sinceramente, este hombre llega a escribir una pagina del porque los hombre lobos existen, y yo le creo sin chistar (contradecir) ni una sola palabra. <br /><br />Nicholas ejerce una atracción como autor de romance en mí, que ningún otro autor a logrado. Y es que no sé como explicarlo, ya que he leído muchas historias de amor las cuales me han gustado, incluso encantado, como es el caso de Yo antes de ti, pero siempre me han hecho sentir como que ese tipo de amor solo ocurren en las novelas, pero la forma de escribir de Sparks hace que crea en ese amor profundo e irracional de una forma muy rara. <br />Ya sé que puede parecer una tontería, pero cada una de sus palabras en sus libros me encantan.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer7150440">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18115222129159751157">I have, in my lifetime, come across so few people that I can honestly say the following about "Straight to a fault". Mr. Sparks steals the cake in this book. Not only does he play up to every hopelessly/sappily romantic notion pop-culture has ever churned out for women over the age of 10, he does this in a sexist/uber macho yet trying to come of as sweet but rough around the edges kind of way. Oh male privilege.... If you want to write from a woman's perspective, you should maybe have the foreth</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18115222129159751157">I have, in my lifetime, come across so few people that I can honestly say the following about "Straight to a fault". Mr. Sparks steals the cake in this book. Not only does he play up to every hopelessly/sappily romantic notion pop-culture has ever churned out for women over the age of 10, he does this in a sexist/uber macho yet trying to come of as sweet but rough around the edges kind of way. Oh male privilege.... If you want to write from a woman's perspective, you should maybe have the forethought to converse with at least one or two about the scenario before jumping headlong into the task. <br />The book was wholly unbelievable, trite and painful to read. I am amazed that movies are made based on this drivel. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_47577765">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47577765" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1710557-bookczuk" class="left imgcol" title="bookczuk"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1228146591p2/1710557.jpg" alt="bookczuk" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/47577765?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 26, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1710557-bookczuk" class="user" title="bookczuk">bookczuk</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15931.The_Notebook" title="Hardcover 9780553816716" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1710557-bookczuk?shelf=bookcrossing" class="actionLinkLite">bookcrossing</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1710557-bookczuk?shelf=met-or-know-the-author" class="actionLinkLite">met-or-know-the-author</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1710557-bookczuk?shelf=set-in-the-south" class="actionLinkLite">set-in-the-south</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1710557-bookczuk?shelf=give-me-my-time-back" class="actionLinkLite">give-me-my-time-back</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer47577765">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15905403211393984152">Someone mentioned to me that she likes that I also review/record books that I've read and don't like. Well, this book is right up there for me. <br /><br />Back when guyczuk was in 4th grade, his teacher came to me one day, saying I <em>had</em> to read this book she'd just read. It was the <em>best book EVER</em> and she stayed up all night to finish it, crying as she read. Being the sort of mother who likes to see what makes her son's 24 year old teacher (who spent more time on the internet planning her upcoming wedding th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15905403211393984152">Someone mentioned to me that she likes that I also review/record books that I've read and don't like. Well, this book is right up there for me. <br /><br />Back when guyczuk was in 4th grade, his teacher came to me one day, saying I <em>had</em> to read this book she'd just read. It was the <em>best book EVER</em> and she stayed up all night to finish it, crying as she read. Being the sort of mother who likes to see what makes her son's 24 year old teacher (who spent more time on the internet planning her upcoming wedding than she did teaching) tick, I borrowed the book.<br /><br />I. Hated. It.<br /><br />Sappy, tugging at your heart-strings, sentimental, pap. Totally unrealistic situation for an Alzheimer's patient, too, and I know from Alzheimer's, trust me. Things just don't happen like that, and I could not be charitable enough to engage the willing suspension of disbelief mode. If the writing had been good, I could have given it credit. But let's not go there.<br /><br />My dislike for the book had 3 consequences:<br /><br />1. I decided to give Sparks one more try. Nope. My opinion didn't change. You've heard of do not call lists? He's on my "do not read" list. I only BookCross copies of his book I've been given. Won't even pick them up second hand.<br /><br />2. When the film of this movie was made here in Charleston, I had the chance to be an extra. As much as I would have liked that experience, I turned it down. And yes, I have NOT seen the movie.<br /><br />3. One day I was in Books-A-Million. There was a huge crowd of women fluttering around an author. He was a clean cut, preppie-ish kind of guy (I remember that his blue shirt had an unfortunate white collar.) When I found out it was Nicholas Sparks, doing a book-signing, I tried to skirt around the crowd. His handler stopped me.<br /><br />"Don't you want to meet the author?"<br /><br />"No thanks," I replied.<br /><br />"But he's rather good. Have you read his books?"<br /><br />"Umm. Yes, but I'd rather not meet him."<br /><br />"You've read his books and don't want to meet him? Why not???"<br /><br />"I'd rather not say," I said, trying to break the iron grip she had on my arm.<br /><br />"He'll sign one for you." <br /><br />"No thank you."<br /><br />At this point, my struggling to get free caught the author's attention. He rose from his signing table, the red sea of women clustering around him parted and he came over to me. He was quite polite, and attentive, and inquired why I was so adamant about not participating in the book signing. Again, I demurred. He insisted. Did I like his book? Well-- no, not exactly. He pushed for details. I'd had enough and let loose with what I thought.<br /><br />To give him credit, he didn't blanch though his handler did, and I actually heard a hiss from one of the ladies in the crowd. He thanked me for my opinion, and said he would rather have someone who vehemently disliked his book that someone who said it was so-so. At least he'd stirred a strong emotion in me. To this day, that is the only thing I like about Nicholas Sparks.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15905403211393984152">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer19655036">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6151572727733778098">I decided to read this book because I absolutely love the movie. It's pretty muc the story of Levi and I, except that we're aren't old yet. He had to kind of convince me to date his, and it was the greatest summer of my life. We were separated by his time at Basic training and his mission to Taiwan. Neither of us had much closure when the relationship had to end. When he returned from his mission I was engaged to someone else, but I had already stated to realize that it wasn't meant to be for he</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6151572727733778098">I decided to read this book because I absolutely love the movie. It's pretty muc the story of Levi and I, except that we're aren't old yet. He had to kind of convince me to date his, and it was the greatest summer of my life. We were separated by his time at Basic training and his mission to Taiwan. Neither of us had much closure when the relationship had to end. When he returned from his mission I was engaged to someone else, but I had already stated to realize that it wasn't meant to be for he and I. I ended the engagement long before I realized that Levi was the one for me. Levi and I were engaged when he'd been home from his mission for a month, and married 6 weeks later.<br /><br />Back to the actual review....I positively adore this movie. Everything about it. So I thought I should read teh book it's based one. And I was disappointed! I like the movie much more. It's so much more descriptive. They are both very passionate characters, and Sparks depicts this is certain ways in the book, but leaves out important ways. Neither seems to have a temper in the book, which I think is part of being passionate. Feeling things strongly. I love that in the movie that are arguing in one anothers' faces on minute and sucking them the next. =o) I can think of several movie moments like this. None in the book. <br /><br />I truly love the love story between the "old" Allie and Noah. It is the <em>true</em> love story, I feel. It is depicted well in both versions, though I like the movie ending better where they die together. In the novel, Sparks seems to focus more on the details of the older couple. I prefer the movie that takes two separate love stories and intertwines them seamlessly. It may be that Sparks wanted to write a love story for "seniors" and Hollywood knew that wouldn't fly and so they added things of their own. But I like Hollywood's version better.<br /><br />I think I remember Nicholas Sparks saying that the movie is how the book should've turned out. I agree. I feel bad saying bad things about it because I love the story so much, I just prefer the movie version better. <br /><br /></span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2664941270280839631">I truly loved this book. The story and how it is told just sucks you in from the minute you start reading. I am amazed over and over again just how much I love this book.<br />I no longer own this book. I lent it to a "friend" and never got it back. And I am having a hard time trying to find a replacement copy. ARGH.<br />This is the story of Noah and Allie. They meet as teens, but are torn apart by circumstances. As the book progresses so do their lives until the moment that Allie realizes she needs to find Noah to put things to rest before she marries a man she likes, but doesn't really love. What happens next is the crux of the novel and proves that love CAN conquer time and space and all the obstacles that others put in its way.<br />GREAT read. I recommend it to anyone!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IFNLGa0pRbfvNAJZ+U91CcybRTeA3ZvsXvLpN6s/dpVFh3TKX/tRTWPsduKHLpO7hWyGLskA3EY0++ylZ6qA0A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }
